                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202000288"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rogach, A. L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anodes and Sodium-Free Cathodes in Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">22</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2000288</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202000288</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D2000288%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D22%26author%3DX.%2BYang%26author%3DA.%2BL.%2BRogach%26title%3DAnodes%2Band%2BSodium-Free%2BCathodes%2Bin%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202000288&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202000288&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anodes and Sodium-Free Cathodes in Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Xuming; Rogach, Andrey L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000288</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increase in electricity generation poses growing demands on energy storage systems, thus offering a chance for the success of the reliable and cost-effective energy storage technologies.  Sodium ion batteries are emerging as such a technol., which is however not yet mature enough to enter the market.  At the crux of building practical sodium ion batteries is the development of electrode materials that promise sufficient cost- and performance-competitiveness.  As such, herein, all typical sodium storage materials are discussed, considering their fabrication methods and sodiation mechanisms in detail.  A comprehensive cross-literature and cross-material comparison, which also includes the related thermodn. anal. of their sodiation products, is also provided.  The review focusses particularly on anodes and sodium-free cathodes, as they both play the role of the acceptor rather than the donor of sodium ions in their operation in batteries; their difference lies in the (de-)sodiation voltage.  In the discussion, special attention is paid to contradictory observations and interpretations in contemporary sodium ion battery research, since debates on these controversies are likely to fuel future sodium battery research.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrwgKXFAPzwjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZsvwSqcXXkw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXnslKhs7c%253D&amp;md5=c74372739d2eae295ff8891b7717cf2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1002/chem.202300009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">SnS-SnO2 Heterostructures Anchored on GO as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium Ion Battery</span>. <i>Chem.─Eur.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dual Regulation of Metal Doping and Adjusting Cut-Off Voltage for MoSe2 to Achieve Reversible Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Xuejiao; Zhu, Ruiyu; Wang, Beibei; Liu, Xiaojie; Wang, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2200437</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoSe2, as a typical 2D material, possesses tremendous potential in Na-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to larger interlayer distance, more favorable band gap structure, and higher theor. specific capacity than other analogs.  Nevertheless, the low intrinsic electronic cond. and irreversible conversion of discharged products of Mo/Na2Se to MoSe2 seriously hamper its electrochem. performance.  Herein, through a facile hydrothermal method combined with calcination process, Sn-doped MoSe2 nanosheets grown on graphene substrate in the vertical direction are fabricated.  Benefiting from the improved electronic cond. contributed by the abundant defects and expanded interlamellar spacing of MoSe2 originated from Sn doping, combined with a smart strategy of raising discharge cut-off voltage to 0.2 V during the actual performance testing for SIBs, the as-fabricated anode material delivers superior Na-ions storage performance in terms of electrons/ions transfer, reversible sodium storage as well as cycle stability.  An ultra-stable reversible specific capacity of 268.5 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 can be maintained after 1600 cycles.  Moreover, the great sodium storage property in the SIB full-cell system of the as-obtained nanocomposite illustrates practical potential.  D. functional theory calcn. and in situ/ex situ measurements are employed to further reveal the storage mechanism and process of Na-ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRtPf4DpHKdbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZsvwSqcXXkw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhsFCrtLrO&amp;md5=8bd2f7427fd0935d401b0cc9138ef50d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201808745"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Peering into Alloy Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Current Trends, Challenges, and Opportunities</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium storage performance of ultrasmall SnSb nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Chao; Pei, Ya Ru; Zhao, Ming; Yang, Chun Cheng; Jiang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">420</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">129617</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have been emerging as a potential alternative to lithium-ion batteries, esp. for large-scale applications.  In this work, a hybrid of ultrasmall SnSb nanoparticles (the diam. &lt;2 nm) encapsulated in three-dimensional N-doped nanoporous carbon frameworks (SnSb/3D-NPC) was synthesized by a facile chem. redn. method.  To the best of our knowledge, this is the smallest SnSb nanoparticle ever reported.  As a sodium-ion battery anode, SnSb/3D-NPC delivers a high reversible capacity (693.6 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 100 cycles), superior rate performance (359.1 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) and cycling stability (266.6 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 15,000 cycles), which outperform other SnSb-based materials.  These remarkable performances originate from: (i) ultrasmall SnSb nanoparticles and their uniform distribution, which increase the sp. surface of electrodes and thus guarantee the full utilization of active materials, enhance pseudocapacitive contributions for Na storage, shorten Na+ diffusion distance, and reduce the strain during the sodiation/desodiation process; and (ii) the unique 3D integrated structure of SnSb/3D-NPC, which supplies a conductive network, efficient electrolyte diffusion paths and more active sites for Na+ insertion/extn., suppresses the aggregation of SnSb nanoparticles, and buffers large vol. change of SnSb through carbon nanocages during the cycling process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryNdOI04t0ubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZsvwSqcXXkw"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acsenergylett.1c02092</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D4336-4344%26journal%3DACS%2BEnergy%2BLett.%26issue%3D12%26author%3DC.%2BWei%26author%3DD.%2BGong%26author%3DD.%2BXie%26author%3DY.%2BTang%26title%3DThe%2BFree-Standing%2BAlloy%2BStrategy%2Bto%2BImprove%2Bthe%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BPotassium-Based%2BDual-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsenergylett.1c02092&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsenergylett.1c02092&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Free-Standing Alloy Strategy to Improve the Electrochemical Performance of Potassium-Based Dual-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wei, Chenyang; Gong, Decai; Xie, Donghao; Tang, Yongbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4336-4344</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2380-8195</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-based dual-ion batteries (PDIBs) have shown good application prospects in large-scale energy storage systems.  However, because of the limited theor. capacity of carbonaceous anodes, the electrochem. performance of PDIBs reported at present is still unsatisfactory.  Employing alloy materials as anodes should be a possible way to improve the capacity of PDIBs.  Herein, free-standing porous carbon nanowires encapsulated with SnSb nanodots (SnSb@PCNWs) are first applied as the anodes for high-performance PDIBs.  The free-standing structure design can reduce the cost and increase the proportion of active materials.  Besides, the SnSb nanodots provide high potassium storage capacity, while the porous carbon nanowires can effectively buffer the vol. expansion of SnSb nanodots.  Consequently, the optimized PDIBs display high capacity of 255.3 mAh g-1 at 2 C (based on anodes), outstanding rate capability up to 12 C, and good cycling performance for 300 cycles at 10 C, which are the best results of the reported PDIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrRgdyP_Ok-7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-Bp2N6QqvqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXisVGrsrvF&amp;md5=9c545ca150546b4925f89880ae66ae34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202002297"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitlin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Review of Emerging Concepts in SEI Analysis and Artificial SEI Membranes for Lithium, Sodium, and Potassium Metal Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">43</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2002297</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202002297</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D2002297%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D43%26author%3DW.%2BLiu%26author%3DP.%2BLiu%26author%3DD.%2BMitlin%26title%3DReview%2Bof%2BEmerging%2BConcepts%2Bin%2BSEI%2BAnalysis%2Band%2BArtificial%2BSEI%2BMembranes%2Bfor%2BLithium%252C%2BSodium%252C%2Band%2BPotassium%2BMetal%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202002297&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202002297&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Review of emerging concepts in solid electrolyte interphase analysis and artificial solid electrolyte interphase membranes for lithium, sodium, and potassium metal battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Wei; Liu, Pengcheng; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2002297</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Anodes for lithium metal batteries, sodium metal batteries, and potassium metal batteries are susceptible to failure due to dendrite growth.  This review details the structure-chem.-performance relations in membranes that stabilize the anodes solid electrolyte interphase (SEI), allowing for stable electrochem. plating/stripping.  Case studies involving Li, Na, and K are presented to illustrate key concepts. "Classical" vs. "modern" understandings of the SEI are described, with an emphasis on the new structural insights obtained through novel anal. techniques, including in situ liq.-secondary ion mass spectroscopy, titrn. gas chromatog., and tip-enhanced Raman spectroscopy.  This Review highlights diverse approaches for increasing SEI stability, either by inserting a secondary layer between the native SEI and the separator, or by combining the membrane with a native SEI to form a hybrid composite.  Exciting and nonintuitive findings are discussed, such as that the metal anode roughness profoundly affects the SEI structure and stability, or that org. artificial SEI-layers may be more effective than the native inorg.-org. SEIs.  Emerging multifunctional architectures are presented, which serve a dual role as metal hosts and metal surface protection layers.  Throughout the Review, fruitful future research directions and the crit. areas where there is incomplete understanding are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoAhCbqYw6U8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-Bp2N6QqvqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvF2jur7L&amp;md5=db6729710066d97907575e4a3559ec35</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202214258"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrostatic Shielding Boosts Electrochemical Performance of Alloy-Type Anode Materials of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                 10.1002/anie.202214258</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D62%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26issue%3D14%26author%3DC.%2BZheng%26author%3DD.%2BJi%26author%3DQ.%2BYao%26author%3DZ.%2BBai%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DC.%2BNie%26author%3DD.%2BLiu%26author%3DN.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DS.%2BDou%26title%3DElectrostatic%2BShielding%2BBoosts%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BAlloy-Type%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bof%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.202214258&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.202214258&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202202939"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Intermolecular Cross-Linking Reinforces Polymer Binders for Durable Alloy-Type Anode Materials of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">9</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2202939</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202202939</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D2202939%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D9%26author%3DQ.%2BYao%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DC.%2BZheng%26author%3DN.%2BWang%26author%3DD.%2BWang%26author%3DF.%2BTian%26author%3DZ.%2BBai%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26author%3DS.%2BDou%26title%3DIntermolecular%2BCross-Linking%2BReinforces%2BPolymer%2BBinders%2Bfor%2BDurable%2BAlloy-Type%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bof%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202202939&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202202939&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intermolecular CrossLinking Reinforces Polymer Binders for Durable Alloy-Type Anode Materials of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yao, Qian; Zhu, Yansong; Zheng, Cheng; Wang, Nana; Wang, Dongdong; Tian, Fang; Bai, Zhongchao; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai; Dou, Shixue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2202939</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries show promising potential for large-scale energy storage.  However, the large size and heavy mass of Na+ always results in huge vol. change and inferior electrochem. stability, esp. in alloy-type anode materials.  Here, mol. engineering of the polymer binders, i.e., crosslinking of poly(acrylic acid) with glycerin (PAA-GLY), reinforces the mech. properties, eliminates the active protons of PAA, and benefits electrolyte diffusion, thereby remarkably improving electrochem. performance.  Using μ-Sn as an example, the cycle life at 2 A g-1 is extended from ≈26 cycles of PAA to ≈2000 cycles of PAA-GLY.  Meanwhile, the initial Coulombic efficiency is promoted to 90.3%, allowing the fabrication step of electrode presodiation for full cells to be eliminated.  Thus, the full cells run 300 cycles at 2 A g-1.  In addn., the binder allows the thick electrode to exhibit an areal capacity of 6.8 mAh cm-2.  This binder is also applied for μ-Bi and μ-Sb.  The simple operation, remarkable improvement, and wide applications indicate the promising prospects of this strategy for advanced electrodes in sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoGTNCqhoL2cbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-Bp2N6QqvqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XjtFSksrbL&amp;md5=4c61f86680f7bc6d53057ffd0e331ab5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/D2CC00833E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bimetallic Bi-Sn microspheres as high initial coulombic efficiency and long lifespan anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>58</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">33</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">5140</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5143</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D2CC00833E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D58%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D5140-5143%26journal%3DChem.%2BCommun.%26issue%3D33%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BCheng%26author%3DQ.%2BYao%26author%3DJ.%2BSu%26author%3DB.%2BChen%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26title%3DBimetallic%2BBi-Sn%2Bmicrospheres%2Bas%2Bhigh%2Binitial%2Bcoulombic%2Befficiency%2Band%2Blong%2Blifespan%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD2CC00833E&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD2CC00833E&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bimetallic Bi-Sn microspheres as high initial coulombic efficiency and long lifespan anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yansong; Wang, Chunting; Cheng, Zhenjie; Yao, Qian; Su, Jie; Chen, Bo; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Communications (Cambridge, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">58</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5140-5143</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHCOFS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1359-7345</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anode materials with a high initial coulombic efficiency and a long lifespan are highly desirable for sodium-ion batteries.  Here, bimetallic μ-BiSn microspheres well combine the high capacity of Sn and the good stability of Bi together, exhibiting superior electrochem. performance, such as a high initial Coulombic efficiency (90.6%), a good cycling stability (541 mA h g-1 after 3000 cycles at 2 A g-1) and an excellent rate capability (393 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoecRcle_UXq7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-Bp2N6QqvqA"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acs.nanolett.2c03334</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D22%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D7976-7983%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26issue%3D19%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DQ.%2BYao%26author%3DR.%2BShao%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26author%3DW.%2BYan%26author%3DJ.%2BMa%26author%3DD.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26title%3DMicrosized%2BGray%2BTin%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BLong-Life%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BAdvanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.2c03334&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.2c03334&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microsized Gray Tin as a High-Rate and Long-Life Anode Material for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yansong; Yao, Qian; Shao, Ruiwen; Wang, Cheng; Yan, Weishan; Ma, Jizhen; Liu, Duo; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7976-7983</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are developed to address the serious concern about the limited resources of lithium.  To achieve high energy d., anode materials with a large specific capacity and a low operation voltage are highly desirable.  Herein, microsized particles of gray Sn (α-Sn) are explored as an anode material of SIBs for the first time.  The distinct structure of α-Sn endows it the reduced vol. change, the improved interaction with polymer binders and the in situ formation of amorphous Sn, as supported by in situ XRD, TEM and DFT calcns.  Therefore, α-Sn exhibits an excellent electrochem. performance, much better than β-Sn widely used before.  Even microsized particles of α-Sn without any treatments deliver a capacity of ~ 451 mAh g-1 after 3500 cycles at 2 A g-1 or ~ 464 mAh g-1 at 4 A g-1 in a rate test.  The results indicate the promising potential of α-Sn in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomNMw5cmJQS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgWGJiFqjYSJA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFShtrjE&amp;md5=632cb9940fdec1f89a9118c0110497d2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.6b00491"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mogensen, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brandell, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Younesi, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solubility of the Solid Electrolyte Interphase (SEI) in Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Energy Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1173</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1178</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solubility of the Solid Electrolyte Interphase (SEI) in Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mogensen, Ronnie; Brandell, Daniel; Younesi, Reza</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1173-1178</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2380-8195</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is often stated that formation of a functional solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) in sodium ion batteries is hampered by the higher soly. of SEI components such as sodium salts in comparison to the lithium analogs.  In order to investigate these phenomena, SEI formation and functionality, as well as cell self-discharge, are studied for the sodium ion system with comparative expts. on the equiv. lithium ion system.  By conducting a set of expts. on carbonaceous anodes, the impact of SEI dissoln. is tested.  The results show that the SEI layer in sodium ion cells is inferior to that in lithium ion counterparts with regards to self-discharge; sodium cells show a loss in capacity at a dramatic rate as compared to the lithium counterparts when they are stored at sodiated and lithiated states, resp., for a long time with no external applied current or potential.  Also, synchrotron-based hard XPS measurements indicate that the major factor leading to increased self-discharge is dissoln. of significant parts of the sodium-based SEI.  Furthermore, the effect of fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) electrolyte additive on self-discharge is tested as part of the work.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokiL-DGoBWJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgWGJiFqjYSJA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvVWnu7nN&amp;md5=efb6371771df6ea383fed6449e8e5e1e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702724"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goktas, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bolli, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Berg, E.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Modulating Electron Conducting Properties at Lithium Anode Interfaces for Durable Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Qi; Zhao, Kaixin; Wang, Jiahui; Xiao, Junpeng; Wu, Lili; Zhang, Xueqiang; Kong, Long; Li, Lu; Lu, Huiqing; Xie, Ying; Li, Wenjie; Zhang, Xitian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">53850-53859</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The lithium (Li) ion and electron diffusion behaviors across the actual solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) play a crit. role in regulating the Li nucleation and growth and improving the performance of lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries.  To date, a no. of researchers have pursued an SEI with high Li-ion cond. while ignoring the Li dendrite growth caused by electron tunneling in the SEI.  Herein, an artificial anti-electron tunneling layer with enriched lithium fluoride (LiF) and sodium fluoride (NaF) nanocrystals is constructed using a facile soln.-soaking method.  As evidenced theor. and exptl., the LiF/NaF artificial SEI exhibits an outstanding electron-blocking capability that can reduce electron tunneling, resulting in dendrite-free and dense Li deposition beneath the SEI, even with an ultrahigh areal capacity.  In addn., the artificial anti-electron tunneling layer exhibits improved ionic cond. and mech. strength, compared to those of routine SEI.  The sym. cells with protected Li electrodes achieve a stable cycling of 1500 h.  The LiF/NaF artificial SEI endows the Li-S full cells with long-term cyclability under conditions of high sulfur loading, lean electrolyte, and limited Li excess.  This study provides a perspective on the design of the SEI for highly safe and practical Li-S batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqbc3CFiePQQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9nZ16hrWcWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XivFWqtrzO&amp;md5=ab01211bcc1b012d6d0be344ef729d9e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.0c12051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electroless Formation of a Fluorinated Li/Na Hybrid Interphase for Robust Lithium Anodes</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electroless Formation of a Fluorinated Li/Na Hybrid Interphase for Robust Lithium Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yingli; Liu, Fangming; Fan, Guilan; Qiu, Xiaoguang; Liu, Jiuding; Yan, Zhenhua; Zhang, Kai; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">143</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2829-2837</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineering a stable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is one of the crit. maneuvers in improving the performance of a lithium anode for high-energy-d. rechargeable lithium batteries.  Herein, we build a fluorinated lithium/sodium hybrid interphase via a facile electroless electrolyte-soaking approach to stabilize the repeated plating/stripping of lithium metal.  Jointed exptl. and computational characterizations reveal that the fluorinated hybrid SEI mainly consisting of NaF, LiF, LixPOyFz, and org. components features a mosaic polycryst. structure with enriched grain boundaries and superior interfacial properties toward Li.  This LiF/NaF hybrid SEI exhibits improved ionic cond. and mech. strength in comparison to the SEI without NaF.  Remarkably, the fluorinated hybrid SEI enables an extended dendrite-free cycling of metallic Li over 1300 h at a high areal capacity of 10 mAh cm-2 in sym. cells.  Furthermore, full cells based on the LiFePO4 cathode and hybrid SEI-protected Li anode sustain long-term stability and good capacity retention (96.70% after 200 cycles) at 0.5 C.  This work could provide a new avenue for designing robust multifunctional SEI to upgrade the metallic lithium anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokydiLqb-nQrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9nZ16hrWcWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXjvFensro%253D&amp;md5=76078582a8c2b9abd2a79cfdeb52e2ec</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202200475"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, P.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, S.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrode-Electrolyte Interfacial Chemistry Modulation for Ultra-High Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode-Electrolyte Interfacial Chemistry Modulation for Ultra-High Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Zheng; Wang, Hong; Wu, Peng-Fei; Zhou, Si-Yu; Huang, Yuan-Cheng; Zhang, Rui; Sun, Dan; Tang, You-Gen; Wang, Hai-Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries capable of operating at rate and temp. extremes are highly desirable, but elusive due to the dynamics and thermodn. limitations.  Herein, a strategy of electrode-electrolyte interfacial chem. modulation is proposed.  The com. hard carbon demonstrates superior rate performance with 212 mAh g-1 at an ultra-high c.d. of 5 A g-1 in the electrolyte with weak ion solvation/desolvation, which is much higher than those in common electrolytes (nearly no capacity in carbonate-based electrolytes).  Even at -20°C, a high capacity of 175 mAh g-1 (74% of its room-temp. capacity) can be maintained at 2 A g-1.  Such an electrode retains 90% of its initial capacity after 1000 cycles.  As proven, weak ion solvation/desolvation of THF greatly facilitates fast-ion diffusion at the SEI/electrolyte interface and homogeneous SEI with well-distributed NaF and org. components ensures fast Na+ diffusion through the SEI layer and a stable interface.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqdIVcdn7NorrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9nZ16hrWcWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xms1yhur8%253D&amp;md5=ea2a3f80a3c080c3cc6276b22f89da3c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201703576"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bommier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolytes, SEI Formation, and Binders: A Review of Nonelectrode Factors for Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Small.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">16</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e1703576</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure and ionic conductivity of the solid electrolyte interphase layer on tin anodes in Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kuo, Liang-Yin; Moradabadi, Ashkan; Huang, Hsin-Fu; Hwang, Bing-Joe; Kaghazchi, Payam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">341</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">107-113</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structure, stability, and ionic cond. of the SEI layer on Sn anodes in Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are studied using exptl. and theor. methods.  Raman spectra show that the SEI layer consists of Na2O and Na2CO3, the latter becoming more dominant close to the discharged state (at 0.3 V).  According to our theor. phase diagrams, Na2O can be stable in the whole voltage range of charge/discharge (from 0.0 V to 1.90 V), but Na2CO3 can decomp. under carbon and/or oxygen poor conditions, leading to the formation of Na2O.  These findings are in agreement with our exptl. cyclic voltammetry and Raman spectra as function of voltage.  Both compds. of the SEI layer have very low ionic cond. close to the discharge state (0.2-0.3 V), but the ionic cond. of Na2O is much larger than that of Na2CO3 for a wide range of voltages from 0.4 V to the charge state (∼1.5 V).  This work suggests that engineered artificial SEI with Na2O or naturally formed SEI in a carbon and/or oxygen poor environment can improve the cond. of the SEI layer in NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpoWK3bL_8N07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgiz6pS2kN2vQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitVSmtb3O&amp;md5=4ed35efcf8022e97010b5d1e378a7141</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1524/zkri.220.5.567.65075"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Clark, S.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">First principles methods using CASTEP</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Clark, Stewart J.; Segall, Matthew D.; Pickard, Chris J.; Hasnip, Phil J.; Probert, Matt I. Comput. Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2006</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>27</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">15</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1787</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1799</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/jcc.20495</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D27%26publication_year%3D2006%26pages%3D1787-1799%26journal%3DJ.%2BComput.%2BChem.%26issue%3D15%26author%3DS.%2BGrimme%26title%3DSemiempirical%2BGGA-type%2Bdensity%2Bfunctional%2Bconstructed%2Bwith%2Ba%2Blong-range%2Bdispersion%2Bcorrection%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fjcc.20495&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fjcc.20495&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Semiempirical GGA-type density functional constructed with a long-range dispersion correction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Grimme, Stefan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Computational Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1787-1799</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCCHDD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0192-8651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new d. functional (DF) of the generalized gradient approxn. (GGA) type for general chem. applications termed B97-D is proposed.  It is based on Becke's power-series ansatz from 1997 and is explicitly parameterized by including damped atom-pairwise dispersion corrections of the form C6·R-6.  A general computational scheme for the parameters used in this correction has been established and parameters for elements up to xenon and a scaling factor for the dispersion part for several common d. functionals (BLYP, PBE, TPSS, B3LYP) are reported.  The new functional is tested in comparison with other GGAs and the B3LYP hybrid functional on std. thermochem. benchmark sets, for 40 noncovalently bound complexes, including large stacked arom. mols. and group II element clusters, and for the computation of mol. geometries.  Further cross-validation tests were performed for organometallic reactions and other difficult problems for std. functionals.  In summary, it is found that B97-D belongs to one of the most accurate general purpose GGAs, reaching, for example for the G97/2 set of heat of formations, a mean abs. deviation of only 3.8 kcal mol-1.  The performance for noncovalently bound systems including many pure van der Waals complexes is exceptionally good, reaching on the av. CCSD(T) accuracy.  The basic strategy in the development to restrict the d. functional description to shorter electron correlation lengths scales and to describe situations with medium to large interat. distances by damped C6·R-6 terms seems to be very successful, as demonstrated for some notoriously difficult reactions.  As an example, for the isomerization of larger branched to linear alkanes, B97-D is the only DF available that yields the right sign for the energy difference.  From a practical point of view, the new functional seems to be quite robust and it is thus suggested as an efficient and accurate quantum chem. method for large systems where dispersion forces are of general importance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodrkmrBLRzxbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgiz6pS2kN2vQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XhtFenu7bO&amp;md5=0b4aa16bebc3a0a2ec175d4b161ab0e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.77.3865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Perdew, J.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Generalized gradient approximation made simple</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Perdew, John P.; Burke, Kieron; Ernzerhof, Matthias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Generalized gradient approxns. (GGA's) for the exchange-correlation energy improve upon the local spin d. (LSD) description of atoms, mols., and solids.  We present a simple derivation of a simple GGA, in which all parameters (other than those in LSD) are fundamental consts.  Only general features of the detailed construction underlying the Perdew-Wang 1991 (PW91) GGA are invoked.  Improvements over PW91 include an accurate description of the linear response of the uniform electron gas, correct behavior under uniform scaling, and a smoother potential.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokga1tVzFw07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgiz6pS2kN2vQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synergistically enhanced sodium/potassium ion storage performance of SnSb alloy particles confined in three-dimensional carbon framework</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Hanqing; Zhuang, Chenfei; Xu, Junmin; Zhang, Zhuangfei; Shen, Weixia; Tang, Haibing; Wang, Ye; Xu, Tingting; Wang, Xinchang; Li, Xinjian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ionics</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Abstr.: In this work, an efficient composite of SnSb alloy particles confined in three-dimensional porous carbon framework (SnSb@C) is rationally designed and fabricated by means of NaCl template-assisted in situ freeze-drying treatment and subsequent thermal redn. method.  Benefit from rational material design and the excellent structural features of the active materials, the SnSb@C can deliver a high initial reversible capacity of 457 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and excellent cycling stability with capacity retention of 84% after 200 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, when evaluated as an anode material for SIBs. These results demonstrated that the SnSb@C composite is a promising anode material for future high-performance SIBs and PIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSoHHHZzAavbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgiz6pS2kN2vQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtF2jurbN&amp;md5=986a18774605f290f55a418230bbcae9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2021.138246"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bimetallic alloy SbSn nanodots filled in electrospun N-doped carbon fibers for high performance Na-ion battery anode</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior electrochemical performance of Sb-Bi alloy for sodium storage: Understanding from alloying element effects and new cause of capacity attenuation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xinxin; Feng, Bin; Huang, Limei; Fu, Qingfeng; Li, Weize; Zhu, Chao; Chen, Peng; Yang, Caili; Ding, Yuan-Li</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">520</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">230826</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-Bi alloy has attracted increased attention as anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its particular crystal structure relevance and synergy effect.  However, the cycle performance and actual capacity of Sb-Bi alloy are still not satisfactory, and the mysteries about partial role of elemental compns. and causes of capacity attenuation remain unsolved either.  Herein, 3D Sb-Bi alloy/N-doped porous carbons (N-PCs) with different Sb/Bi mole ratios have been synthesized successfully.  As for SIB anodes, 3D Bi3Sb1/N-PC presents a superior rate capability up to 30 A g-1 (specific capacity: 318.3 mAh g-1) and cyclic stability (capacity decays: 0.0054% per cycle at 10 A g-1 after 6000 cycles).  Furthermore, the dissoln. behavior of metallic Sb can be found after long-term cycles with DME-based electrolyte, and the dissolved Sb can shuttle to the other side of the separators, leading to "dead antimony" with low specific capacity and unsatisfactory cycle performance.  Notably, Bi crystal shows strong fixing effect on Sb atoms with low loss of "active antimony".  Our work presents a great potential of alloy-type anode materials for practical applications of high-energy SIBs, and also provide a new direction to analyze element roles and attenuation causes of Sb-Bi alloys for sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXzqiXWOi_9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEFAD99jowAw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Alloyed bismuth antimony nanoparticles confined in tremella-like carbon microspheres for ultralong-life potassium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Chuyun; Xu, Anding; Li, Guilan; Sun, Hao; Wu, Songping; Xu, Zhiguang; Yan, Yurong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2100685</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth-antimony alloy is considered as a promising potassium ion battery anode because of its combination of the high theor. capacity of antimony and the excellent rate capacity of bismuth.  However, the large vol. change and sluggish reaction kinetic upon cycling have triggered severe capacity fading and poor rate performance.  Herein, a nanoconfined BiSb in tremella-like carbon microspheres (BiSb@TCS) are delicately designed to address these issues.  As-prepd. BiSb@TCS renders an outstanding potassium-storage performance with a reversible capacity of 181 mAh g-1 after ultralong 5700 cycles at a c.d. of 2 A g-1, and an excellent rate capacity of 119.3 mAh g-1 at 6 A g-1.  Such a superior performance can be ascribed to the delicate microstructure.  The self-assembled carbon microspheres can strengthen integral structure and effectively accommodate the vol. expansion of BiSb nanoparticles, and 2D carbon nanowalls in carbon microspheres can provide fast ion/electron diffusion dynamic.  Theor. calcn. also suggests a thermodn. feasibility of alloyed BiSb nanoparticles for storing potassium ion.  Such a work shows that BiSb@TCS possesses a great potential to be a high-performance anode of potassium ion batteries.  The rational designing of multiscaled structure would be instructive to the exploitation of other energy-storage materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqeu3NqSRZEc7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEFAD99jowAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXps1Khur4%253D&amp;md5=ce408f974d7886bb67a3ed8588c49b08</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202009433"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A General Strategy for Antimony-Based Alloy Nanocomposite Embedded in Swiss-Cheese-Like Nitrogen-Doped Porous Carbon for Energy Storage</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>31</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">13</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2009433</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202009433</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D31%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D2009433%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D13%26author%3DT.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhong%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BYuan%26author%3DD.%2BYang%26author%3DQ.%2BMao%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DA%2BGeneral%2BStrategy%2Bfor%2BAntimony-Based%2BAlloy%2BNanocomposite%2BEmbedded%2Bin%2BSwiss-Cheese-Like%2BNitrogen-Doped%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2Bfor%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202009433&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202009433&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A General Strategy for Antimony-Based Alloy Nanocomposite Embedded in Swiss-Cheese-Like Nitrogen-Doped Porous Carbon for Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Tao; Zhong, Jiasong; Liu, Jianwen; Yuan, Yongjun; Yang, Dexin; Mao, Qinan; Li, Xinyue; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2009433</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to its suitable working voltage and high theor. storage capacity, antimony is considered a promising neg. electrode material for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and has attracted widespread attention.  The vol. effect during cycling, however, will cause the antimony anode to undergo a severe structural collapse and a rapid decrease in capacity.  Here, a general in situ self-template-assisted strategy is proposed for the rational design and prepn. of a series of M-Sb (M = Ni, Co, or Fe) nanocomposites with M-N-C coordination, which are firmly anchored on Swiss-cheese-like nitrogen-doped porous carbon as anodes for LIBs.  The large interface pore network structure, the introduction of heteroatoms, and the formation of strong metal-N-C bonds effectively enhance their electronic cond. and structural integrity, and provide abundant interfacial lithium storage.  The exptl. results have proved the high rate performance and excellent cycling stability of antimony-based composite materials.  Electrochem. kinetics studies have demonstrated that the increase in capacity during cycling is mainly controlled by the diffusion mechanism rather than the pseudocapacitance contribution.  This facile strategy can provide a new pathway for low-cost and high-yield synthesis of Sb-based composites with high performance, and is expected to be applied in other energy-related fields such as sodium-/potassium-ion batteries or electrocatalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokQqRsbkMzdLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEFAD99jowAw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controllable Synthesis of Peapod-like Sb@C and Corn-like C@Sb Nanotubes for Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Kaixuan; Tang, Jianfeng; Liu, Yan; Kong, Ming; Zhou, Bin; Shang, Yongchen; Zhang, Wen-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5728-5737</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is regarded as an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  Combining Sb with carbonaceous materials has been considered as an effective way to resolve the serious vol. expansion issues.  Sb/C composites mainly consist of two types, i.e., Sb confined inside a carbon matrix and Sb deposited on the surface of a carbon matrix, and both have shown superior sodium storage performance.  However, which structure is more beneficial for achieving high electrochem. performance is still unclear.  In this work, peapod-like Sb@C and corn-like C@Sb nanotubes are synthesized via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement reaction and used as model materials for sodium storage to explore the above issue.  When evaluated as anode materials for SIBs, the peapod-like Sb@C shows a higher rate capability and a significantly better long-term cycling stability compared to those of the corn-like C@Sb.  Electrochem. anal. reveals that the peapod-like Sb@C exhibits faster Na+ and electron transport kinetics and higher proportions of surface capacitive contributions.  These results demonstrate the structural superiority of the nanoconfined structure and provide valuable information for the rational design and construction of Sb-based anode materials for high-performance electrochem. energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoffTaOrNgQZrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3gAcO40YRjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXnslehsrw%253D&amp;md5=17554b3d1ee580321731a053ddf5e39c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202104798"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Localized Electron Density Redistribution in Fluorophosphate Cathode: Dangling Anion Regulation and Enhanced Na-Ion Diffusivity for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jinjin; Kang, Jinzhao; Gu, Zhen-Yi; Liang, Qinghua; Zhao, Xiangyuan; Wang, Xiaomei; Guo, Ruisheng; Yu, Hong; Du, Cheng-Feng; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2109694</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Polyanionic transition metal polyphosphate (TMPO)-type Na3V2(PO4)2O2F (NVPO2F) is promising as cathode for large-scale sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) on account of its considerable capacity and highly stable structure.  However, the redox of transition metal and phase transitions along with the (de)intercalation of Na+ lead to its slow kinetics and inferior rate performance.  Herein, chlorine (Cl) is applied as a heteropical dopant to obtain Cl-doped NVPO2F (NVPO2-xClxF) cathode material for SIBs.  D. functional theory investigation reveals that Cl doping tunes the localized electronic d. and structure in NVPO2F lattice, causing the electron redistribution on vanadium center and dangling anions.  Hence, the NVPO2-xClxF cathode exhibits a revised redox behavior of vanadium for Na+ extn./insertion, increases Na+ diffusion rate, as well as lowers charge transfer resistance.  A Na+ storage mechanism of reversible transformations between three phases and V4+/V5+ redox couple for NVPO2-xClxF cathode is verified.  The NVPO2-xClxF cathode reveals a high rate capacity of ∼63 mAh g-1 at 30C and great cycle stability over 1000 cycles at 10C.  More importantly, outstanding rate property (314 Wh kg-1 at 5850 W kg-1) and cycling capability are obtained for the NVPO2-xClxF//3DC@Se full cell.  This study demonstrates a brand-new strategy to prep. advanced cathode materials for superior SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqjl-sGlJVatLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3gAcO40YRjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXisVOlt77F&amp;md5=d5e199ec40d0b921579eddbb63672927</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA02248H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fehse, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M.
