Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">18</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">8724</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">8734</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8TA02248H</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D8724-8734%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26issue%3D18%26author%3DM.%2BFehse%26author%3DM.%2BT.%2BSougrati%26author%3DA.%2BDarwiche%26author%3DV.%2BGabaudan%26author%3DC.%2BLa%2BFontaine%26author%3DL.%2BMonconduit%26author%3DL.%2BStievano%26title%3DElucidating%2Bthe%2Borigin%2Bof%2Bsuperior%2Belectrochemical%2Bcycling%2Bperformance%253A%2Bnew%2Binsights%2Bon%2Bsodiation-desodiation%2Bmechanism%2Bof%2BSnSb%2Bfrom%2Boperando%2Bspectroscopy%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC8TA02248H&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC8TA02248H&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Elucidating the origin of superior electrochemical cycling performance: new insights on sodiation-desodiation mechanism of SnSb from operando spectroscopy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fehse, Marcus; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Darwiche, Ali; Gabaudan, Vincent; La Fontaine, Camille; Monconduit, Laure; Stievano, Lorenzo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8724-8734</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As it has been recently shown in the literature, SnSb exhibits better performance in Na-ion than in Li-ion batteries in spite of its even larger vol. expansion.  Where is this special behavior coming from.  In this work, the reversible sodiation-desodiation reaction of SnSb was investigated by simultaneous operando Sn and Sb K-edge X-ray absorption spectroscopy along with operando119Sn M.ovrddot.ossbauer spectroscopy.  Chemometric tools such as principal component anal. and multivariate curve resoln. - alternating least squares were used to analyze the whole data sets to gain information on the nature and sequence of formation of different species during electrochem. cycling vs. Na.  The obtained results indicate that the sodiation reaction is a two-step process clearly distinct from the reaction of SnSb vs. Li.  Firstly Sb is sodiated to form Na3Sb and an intermediate phase of nanosized metallic Sn, which we were able to identify as α-Sn, commonly unstable at ambient conditions.  During the second step, this tin phase is fully sodiated to form Na15Sn4, as rarely obsd. for pure Sn-based electrodes.  Finally, EXAFS anal. proves that the amorphous SnSb phase formed after one complete cycle is clearly distinct from the pristine material.  These new insights on the mechanism of SnSb vs. Na provide a basis for understanding the exceptional electrochem. performance, which is superior not only to SnSb vs. Li but also to Sn vs. Na.  The key to the enhanced cycle life and capacity retention lies in the gradual formation of amorphous, nano-confined intermediate phases and correlated elastic softening of highly sodiated tin and antimony phases which have enhanced ability to absorb and mitigate the strong vol. changes occurring upon sodiation and desodiation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgrdGlUamCXrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3gAcO40YRjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXns1ersbk%253D&amp;md5=474b2eb1237ae8e54cec95f5adc65bb7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1021/acsanm.0c03155"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Composites of SnSb Nanoparticles Embedded in Porous Carbon Nanofibers Wrapped with Reduced Graphene Oxide for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Nano Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">826</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">833</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsanm.0c03155</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D826-833%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BNano%2BMater.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DZ.%2BYuan%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DG.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BYang%26author%3DL.%2BDong%26author%3DX.%2BYu%26title%3DComposites%2Bof%2BSnSb%2BNanoparticles%2BEmbedded%2Bin%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2BNanofibers%2BWrapped%2Bwith%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsanm.0c03155&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.4c03240&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsanm.0c03155&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Composites of SnSb Nanoparticles Embedded in Porous Carbon Nanofibers Wrapped with Reduced Graphene Oxide for Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Zhaoxia; Wang, Luwen; Wang, Gaofeng; Yang, Zunxian; Dong, Linxi; Yu, Xuebin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Nano Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">826-833</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AANMF6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2574-0970</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Alloying-type anode materials are hopeful candidates for sodium (Na)-ion batteries (SIBs) because of their high theor. capacity by forming Na-rich intermetallic compds.  However, the huge vol. changes lead to serious aggregation and crushing of active materials during the cycling process, resulting in a rapid decay in the capacity of the electrode materials.  Herein, we report the manuf. of reduced graphene oxide wrapped on the surface of tin-antimony/nitrogen-doped porous carbon nanofibers (SnSb/N-PCNFs/rGO) by a coaxial electrospinning technique and subsequent annealing treatment.  The cooperative effect of rGO and PCNFs can greatly relieve the vol. expansion of the SnSb alloy in the cycling process and offer more insertion sites for Na+ ions, thus significantly improving the electrochem. performance.  As a SIB anode, the SnSb/N-PCNFs/rGO composite exhibits better reversible capacity (maintaining 416 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 120 cycles), excellent rate performance, and marvelous cycle performance (up to 303 mAh g-1 at 2000 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles), making it a hopeful anode candidate for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo4EbcjY4cFSLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3gAcO40YRjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXptVOnsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=89750a6741d25ba30ca788e05762d8d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.9b01660"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Galvanic Replacement Synthesis of Highly Uniform Sb Nanotubes: Reaction Mechanism and Enhanced Sodium Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yan; Zhou, Bin; Liu, Sheng; Ma, Qingshan; Zhang, Wen-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5885-5892</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">One-dimensional nanotubes are very useful for achieving excellent performance in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to the fact that tubular structures can effectively alleviate the structural strain and shorten the ion diffusion length during repeated cycling.  The authors report a Cu2Sb-mediated growth strategy to controllably fabricate highly uniform Sb nanotubes (NTs), as well as Cu@Cu2Sb and Cu2Sb@Sb composite NTs, via a facile galvanic replacement reaction using Cu nanowires (NWs) as sacrificial templates. Also, a full cell with Sb NTs as anode and Na3(VOPO4)2F as cathode exhibits a high energy d. (252 Wh/kg) and high output voltage (2.7 V), revealing their significant application promise in the next-generation SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYI1QNjiYgqLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liF1XIGpHYaWA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unveiling the microscopic origin of asymmetric phase transformations in (de)sodiated Sb2Se3 with in situ transmission electron microscopy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Yi; Luo, Wen; Gao, Peng; Zhu, Chongyang; Hu, Xiaobing; Qu, Ke; Chen, Jing; Wang, Yuqiao; Sun, Litao; Mai, Liqiang; Xu, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">77</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">105299</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have huge application potential in large-scale energy storage systems due to high abundance and low cost of sodium resource.  Metal chalcogenides, which store Na ions by multiple reactions of intercalation, conversion, and alloying, are considered promising anode materials with high theor. capacity but often suffer from fast capacity fading and underlying reason remains elusive due to the lack of a precise understanding of microscopic behaviors.  Here, combined with in situ high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy and consecutive electron diffraction, we tracked phase transformations during (de)sodiation of Sb2Se3 nanowires in real time and revealed multi-step reaction mechanisms.  During sodiation, Sb2Se3 NWs firstly underwent the intercalation of Na ions and forming NaxSb2Se3 phase, following by the conversion reaction into Na2Se and Sb phases; afterwards, metallic Sb could further alloy with Na to form Na3Sb phase via sequential intermediate NaxSb phases.  While during desodiation, despite the reversible dealloying of Na3Sb phase, the following deconversion of Na2Se and Sb phases back to Sb2Se3 phase was incomplete, which is deemed to be the key factor causing rapid capacity decay.  Furthermore, we reveal that contact interfaces between NWs greatly affected the degree of deconversion reaction due to possibly changed electrode reaction kinetics.  This work not only reports the first exptl. visualization proof showing the effect of contact interfaces on phase transformations of electrode materials, but also affords new insights into capacity decay mechanisms and rational design of high-capacity SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqq2tS_Wdl9nbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liF1XIGpHYaWA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhslejt7rL&amp;md5=d1d7506867c25916ffb617d7d580b16b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1002/ente.201900389"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brehm, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Buchheim, J.                         cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoscale localized growth of SnSb for general-purpose high performance alkali (Li, Na, K) ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Xuejian; Liu, Wanqiang; Zhang, Dongyu; Wang, Chunli; Zhao, Jianxun; Wang, Xinwei; Chen, Bingbing; Chang, Limin; Cheng, Yong; Wang, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">431</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_3</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this paper, we have successfully encapsulated SnSb alloy nanoparticles into the space of N-doped carbon nanotubes and carbon shells (NC@SnSb@NC) like a three-dimensional (3D) corn-like structure via a unique method, showing excellent electrochem. storage performance for alkali metal-ion batteries.  Here, Sn and Sb can be alloyed with alkali metal ions (Li+/Na+/K+) at different potentials, which can serve as a buffer substrate for each other and inhibit the pulverization of active materials.  Pyridine N and pyrrole N in the composite can produce abundant external defects and active sites, which are conducive to accelerating the transmission of alkali metal ions (Li+/Na+/K+).  The available space derived from the carbon nanotubes and carbon shells also can effectively alleviate vol. change, making high mech. flexibility and keeping the whole electrode integrity during charge and discharge process.  In-situ, ex-situ characterizations and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. collectively confirm the excellent reversibility of alkali metal ions storage and fast electrochem. kinetics of the 3D NC@SnSb@NC composite.  Due to the outstanding electrochem. properties, the NC@SnSb@NC composite can be of great significance for practical design and application in next-generation alkali metal-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4ORsSM4Bz0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liF1XIGpHYaWA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisVCjsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=8394e8c16aa402ec0af521d4135e1b7e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2024.04.208"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fluorine-ion-regulated yolk-shell carbon-silicon anode material for high performance lithium ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quantitative chemistry in electrolyte solvation design for aqueous batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Leilei; Cheng, Haoran; Zhang, Junli; Guo, Yingjun; Sun, Chunsheng; Zhou, Min; Li, Qian; Ma, Zheng; Ming, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1076-1095</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Aq. electrolyte design is pivotal for boosting the energy d. and lifespan of aq. batteries, because it can expand the electrochem. stability window and also mitigate the parasitic side reactions.  Until now, three main kinds of electrolytes, i.e., water-in-salt, eutectic, and additives-modified electrolytes, have been developed by which the activity of H2O can be lowered and/or the formed specific solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) can mitigate the decompn. of H2O.  However, there is still a lack of a universal model to elucidate the reason for the improved performance, esp. as the SEI interpretation becomes ever more controversial.  Herein, we present a quant. and graphical model of the electrolyte solvation structure and metal-ion (de)solvation process (i.e., interfacial model) to summarize a relationship between the electrolyte-electrode interfacial chem. and electrode performance.  This Focus Review extends the solvation structure and interfacial model into the field of aq. electrolytes, revealing the essential influence of the solvation structure's properties on electrolyte stability and electrode performance, by which electrode performance and electrolyte design can be more quant. and accurately understood.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqUp9vlJPOPBbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liF1XIGpHYaWA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-enhanced centrifugally-spun SnSb/carbon microfiber composite as advanced anode material for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jia, Hao; Dirican, Mahmut; Aksu, Cemile; Sun, Na; Chen, Chen; Zhu, Jiadeng; Zhu, Pei; Yan, Chaoyi; Li, Ya; Ge, Yeqian; Guo, Jiansheng; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">536</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">655-663</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony tin (SnSb) based materials have become increasingly attractive as a potential anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to their prominent merit of high capacity.  However, cyclic stability and rate capability of SnSb anodes are currently hindered by their large vol. change during repeated cycling, which results in severe capacity fading.  Herein, we introduce carbon-coated centrifugally-spun SnSb@carbon microfiber (CMF) composites as high-performance anodes for SIBs that can maintain their structural stability during repeated charge-discharge cycles.  The centrifugal spinning method was performed to fabricate SnSb@CMFs due to its high speed, low cost, and large-scale fabrication features.  More importantly, extra carbon coating by chem. vapor deposition (CVD) has been demonstrated as an effective method to improve the capacity retention and Coulombic efficiency of the SnSb@CMF anode.  Electrochem. test results indicated that the as-prepd. SnSb@CMF@C anode could deliver a large reversible capacity of 798 mA h•g-1 at the 20th cycle as well as a high capacity retention of 86.8% and excellent Coulombic efficiency of 98.1% at the 100th cycle.  It is, therefore, demonstrated that SnSb@CMF@C composite is a promising anode material candidate for future high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqRqbXkmXhQbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6SHfHBINgBg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitVygs7bK&amp;md5=16605aacb122675332f7b4e57b2397b2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref61'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202206340"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anion-Vacancy Modified WSSe Nanosheets on 3D Cross-Networked Porous Carbon Skeleton for Non-Aqueous Sodium-Based Dual-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Small.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">10</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2206340</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-capacity Sb2SnO5 with controlled Sb/Sn phase modulation as advanced anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xiaojing; Zhang, Ning; He, Pengfei; Ding, Xuli</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">938</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">168472</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Low cost and considerable theory specific capacity (∼1195 mAh g-1) make Sb2SnO5 (SSO) material becoming a potential candidate for sodium-ions battery anodes.  However, the low electronic cond. and sluggish ions transfer kinetic has inhibited the practical applications.  Herein, we demonstrate a novel Sn/Sb@SSO@PCFs composite using simple but effective electrospinning methods, which enable SSO nanoparticles embedded with Sn and Sb nanodomains in situ generation.  The SSO was first reported as anode for sodium-ion batteries and in situ generation Sb and Sn nanocrystals domain around the SSO oxides.  Different from existing tactics, the unique composite establishes a robust and efficient elec. contact between the SSO and the conductive Sb and Sn phases, enabling fast ions and electrons transfer across the electrochem. active SSO/Sb/Sn.  Meanwhile, the composites offer an opportunity to compromise the challenges faced by each entity and enhance the overall performance by circumventing the weakness of individual SSO, Sn and Sb.  As evidenced, the as-fabricated composite has unexpected electrochem. properties, including high capacity and long cycle stability with a retention rate of 83% after 450 cycles at 0.5 C.  Combined with synergistic Na+ ions storage of SSO/Sb/Sb and a simple and scalable manufg. process, this study provides a new strategy to modulate material delivering high capacity and cycle stability for the next generation sodium ions batteries (SIBs).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp79th71tPTDbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6SHfHBINgBg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XjtFyjsbfL&amp;md5=23ef958e52ae7658a13146160fe4c466</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref64'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201770072"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, J.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Z.                         cas_cit65R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">65</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Harnessing Plasma-Assisted Doping Engineering to Stabilize Metallic Phase MoSe2 for Fast and Durable Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Hanna; Zhang, Hehe; Huang, Dan; Kuang, Wei; Li, Xiaolong; Hao, Junnan; Guo, Zaiping; Zhang, Chuhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2200397</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic-phase selenide molybdenum (1T-MoSe2) has become a rising star for sodium storage in comparison with its semiconductor phase (2H-MoSe2) owing to the intrinsic metallic electronic cond. and unimpeded Na+ diffusion structure.  However, the thermodynamically unstable nature of 1T phase renders it an unprecedented challenge to realize its phase control and stabilization.  Herein, a plasma-assisted P-doping-triggered phase-transition engineering is proposed to synthesize stabilized P-doped 1T phase MoSe2 nanoflower composites (P-1T-MoSe2 NFs).  Mechanism anal. reveals significantly decreased phase-transition energy barriers of the plasma-induced Se-vacancy-rich MoSe2 from 2H to 1T owing to its low crystallinity and reduced structure stability.  The vacancy-rich structure promotes highly concd. P doping, which manipulates the electronic structure of the MoSe2 and urges its phase transition, acquiring a high transition efficiency of 91% accompanied with ultrahigh phase stability.  As a result, the P-1T-MoSe2 NFs deliver an exceptional high reversible capacity of 510.8 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 with no capacity fading over 1000 cycles at 5000 mA g-1 for sodium storage.  The underlying mechanism of this phase-transition engineering verified by profound anal. provides informative guide for designing advanced materials for next-generation energy-storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRYUnUOkAYh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6SHfHBINgBg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium (Li) metal anode coupled with high-voltage cathode is crit. for realizing high-energy storage.  However, the org.-dominated solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) originating from carbonate electrolytes undergoes continuous cracking/reformation during cycling, leading to severe Li dendrite growth that hinders its practical application.  Herein, we report an extremely sol. ionic liq. salt of pyridinium trifluoroacetate for constructing inorg.-rich SEI on Li in com. carbonate electrolytes.  Pyridinium cations (Py+) could be attached to the neg.-charged surface of Li due to electrostatic interaction and thereafter be decompd. into Li+-conductive nitrogen-contg. components.  Moreover, benefiting from the strong coordination of carbonyl (C=O) and Li+, trifluoroacetate anions (TFA-) can prompt the dissoln. of lithium nitrate (LiNO3) in carbonate electrolytes, thereby tuning the Li+ solvated shell.  The formation of distinct solvation shell involving abundant anions is exptl. and theor. demonstrated, which favors rapid desolvation kinetics.  In addn., combined effect of additives facilitates the formation of additive-derived LiF-Li3N enhanced inorg.-rich SEI, significantly reducing the Li+ diffusion energy barrier and promoting compact chunky Li deposition.  A thin and dense cathode electrolyte interphase (CEI) layer is generated in designed electrolyte and restrains dissoln. of transition-metals.  Consequently, superior cycling and rate performance of Li||NCM523 cells is achieved, confirming the enhanced stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-y34IwrdlPLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6SHfHBINgBg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xis1yqurnP&amp;md5=6311d46412020ed79488905ce2d578cb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref67"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref67'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">67</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit67" data-doi="10.1109/TTE.2020.3028475"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Knapp, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ehrenberg, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Low-Temperature Separating Lithium-Ion Battery Interfacial Polarization Based on Distribution of Relaxation Times (DRT) of Impedance</span>. <i>IEEE T.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ether based electrolytes have surfaced as alternatives to conventional carbonates allowing for enhanced electrochem. performance of sodium-ion batteries; however, the primary source of the improvement remains poorly understood.  Here we show that coupling titanium dioxide and other anode materials with diglyme does enable higher efficiency and reversible capacity than those for the combination involving ester electrolytes.  Importantly, the electrolyte dependent performance is revealed to be the result of the different structural evolution induced by a varied sodiation depth.  A suit of characterizations show that the energy barrier to charge transfer at the interface between electrolyte and electrode is the factor that dominates the interfacial electrochem. characteristics and therefore the energy storage properties.  Our study proposes a reliable parameter to assess the intricate sodiation dynamics in sodium-ion batteries and could guide the design of aprotic electrolytes for next generation rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5MBNg2cK80rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWmq1tEIukpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXns1Gitbk%253D&amp;md5=3f7a4525b81e73f745c4efb6bc980ab3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref70"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref70'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">70</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit70" data-doi="10.1021/cr500003w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolytes and Interphases in Li-Ion Batteries and Beyond</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit71R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">71</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Excellent Cycling Stability of Sodium Anode Enabled by a Stable Solid Electrolyte Interphase Formed in Ether-Based Electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Le, Phung M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have been considered one of the most promising power sources beyond Li-ion batteries.  Although the Na metal anode exhibits a high theor. capacity of 1165 mAh g-1, its application in Na batteries is largely hindered by dendrite growth and low coulombic efficiency.  Herein, it is demonstrated that an electrolyte consisting of 1 M sodium tetrafluoroborate in tetraglyme can enable excellent cycling efficiency (99.9%) of a Na metal anode for more than 1000 cycles.  This high reversibility of a Na anode can be attributed to a stable solid electrolyte interphase formed on the Na surface, as revealed by cryogenic transmission electron microscopy and XPS.  These electrolytes also enable excellent cycling stability of Na||hard-carbon cells and Na||Na2/3Co1/3Mn2/3O2 cells at high rates with very high coulombic efficiencies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq6D6Ot3zypnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWmq1tEIukpA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit73R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">73</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Impact of the salts and solvents on the SEI formation in Sb/Na batteries: An XPS analysis</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Bodenes, Lucille; Madec, Lenaic; Monconduit, Laure; Martinez, Herve</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A thorough XPS is carried out on the Sb/Na electrochem. cell to rationalize the different electrochem. performances in terms of irreversible capacity on 1st cycle, cumulated capacity losses, reversible capacity and capacity retention.  Surface anal. of Sb electrode cycled vs. Na using three different electrolyte formulations by changing the nature of (NaClO4 or NaPF6) and the nature of the solvents (PC or EC/DMC mixt.) was performed by a combined XPS core peaks and quantification data anal. to establish the main components of the solid electrolyte interphase film (SEI) and its evolution on cycling.  The passivation layer formed during cycling is mainly constituted of carbonates, Na2CO3 and alkylcarbonates, that appear during the discharge after the preferential deposition of NaF from the degrdn. of FEC.  The solvent appears to have a key role, and the NaClO4/PC electrolyte, despite the high viscosity of its solvent gives the best compromise in terms of performances by forming a stable and thick SEI at the surface of all components of the composite electrode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrDy_xYF3XIrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWmq1tEIukpA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit74R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">74</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Analysis of the Stable Interphase Responsible for the Excellent Electrochemical Performance of Graphite Electrodes in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Zhaohua; Yang, Haoyi; Liu, Yiran; Bai, Ying; Chen, Guanghai; Li, Ying; Wang, Xinran; Xu, Huajie; Wu, Chuan; Lu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2003268</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considerable efforts have been exerted to understand the formation and properties of the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) in sodium ion batteries.  However, the puzzling existence and role of SEI behind the huge vol. changes of the graphite electrodes need to be answered.  Herein, the reason of how ether-derived SEI maintains excellent reversibility despite the huge vol. changes during cycling is unraveled.  Theor. simulations and Fourier-transform IR spectroscopy demonstrate the formation mechanism of an SEI between the graphite anode and electrolyte.  Furthermore, the high mech. tolerance of the ether-derived SEI is confirmed in at. force microscopy.  A depth profile of XPS points to a multilayer structure of the ether-derived SEI.  The outer layer comprises orgs. (sodium alkoxide), while the inorgs. (Na2CO3, NaF) in interior region are mixed with some orgs.  Notably, the presence of orgs. ensures the adaptability of the SEI to the vol. expansion of graphite during cycling, and the concd. distribution of inorgs. improves the Young's modulus (resistance to deformation).  Therefore, the graphite anode exhibits high cycle stability (96.6% capacity retention ratio at 1 A g-1 over 860 cycles) and efficiency (≈99.5%).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6VJ3B-G7caLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWmq1tEIukpA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit75R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">75</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mitigating Electron Leakage of Solid Electrolyte Interface for Stable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Enhui; Wan, Jing; Guo, Yu-Jie; Zhang, Qianyu; He, Wei-Huan; Zhang, Chao-Hui; Chen, Wan-Ping; Yan, Hui-Juan; Xue, Ding-Jiang; Fang, Tiantian; Wang, Fuyi; Wen, Rui; Xin, Sen; Yin, Ya-Xia; Guo, Yu-Guo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">62</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The interfacial stability is highly responsible for the longevity and safety of sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the continuous solid-electrolyte interphase(SEI) growth would deteriorate its stability.  Essentially, the SEI growth is assocd. with the electron leakage behavior, yet few efforts have tried to suppress the SEI growth, from the perspective of mitigating electron leakage.  Herein, we built two kinds of SEI layers with distinct growth behaviors, via the additive strategy.  The SEI physicochem. features (morphol. and componential information) and SEI electronic properties (LUMO level, band gap, electron work function) were investigated elaborately.  Exptl. and calculational analyses showed that, the SEI layer with suppressed growth delivers both the low electron driving force and the high electron insulation ability.  Thus, the electron leakage is mitigated, which restrains the continuous SEI growth, and favors the interface stability with enhanced electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a         </div><div class="casAbstract">The large-scale application of sodium ion batteries (SIBs) is limited by economic and environmental factors.  Here, we prep. multi-heteroatom self-doped hierarchical porous carbon (HHPC) with a honeycomb-like structure by one-step carbonization method using high-yield and low-cost biomass silkworm excrement as a precursor.  As an anode for SIB, HHPC-1100 exhibits a capacity of 331.7 mA h g-1 at 20 mA g-1, while it also reveals remarkable rate performance and stable long cycle capability due to its abundant pore structure and proper amt. of hetero atom doping.  Moreover, the synergistic effect of O, N, S, P co-doping in carbon materials on sodium ion adsorption is verified by the first-principles study, which provide a theor. basis for the prominent electrochem. performance of the material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJZhL_75liRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljc8M0MKrTxTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFKqtbvE&amp;md5=cfecef0907bf2bfe4d8fa8913ed7b366</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1038/s41578-021-00324-w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Usiskin, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Popovic, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Law, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Balaya, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maier, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fundamentals, status and promise of sodium-based batteries</span>. <i>Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A Review.  Na-based batteries have shown substantial progress in recent years and are promising candidates for mitigating the supply risks assocd. with Li-based batteries.  In this Review, Na and Li batteries are compared in terms of fundamental principles and specific materials.  Principles for the rational design of a Na battery architecture are discussed.  Recent prototypes are surveyed to demonstrate that Na cells offer realistic alternatives that are competitive with some Li cells in terms of performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpj2gonMRam5LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljc8M0MKrTxTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXitVylsrvJ&amp;md5=1e54612b457e9094f3883f72d280abab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702582"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hasa, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Beyond Insertion for Na-Ion Batteries: Nanostructured Alloying and Conversion Anode Materials</span>. <i>Adv. L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anodes and Sodium-Free Cathodes in Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">22</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2000288</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202000288</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anodes and Sodium-Free Cathodes in Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Xuming; Rogach, Andrey L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000288</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increase in electricity generation poses growing demands on energy storage systems, thus offering a chance for the success of the reliable and cost-effective energy storage technologies.  Sodium ion batteries are emerging as such a technol., which is however not yet mature enough to enter the market.  At the crux of building practical sodium ion batteries is the development of electrode materials that promise sufficient cost- and performance-competitiveness.  As such, herein, all typical sodium storage materials are discussed, considering their fabrication methods and sodiation mechanisms in detail.  A comprehensive cross-literature and cross-material comparison, which also includes the related thermodn. anal. of their sodiation products, is also provided.  The review focusses particularly on anodes and sodium-free cathodes, as they both play the role of the acceptor rather than the donor of sodium ions in their operation in batteries; their difference lies in the (de-)sodiation voltage.  In the discussion, special attention is paid to contradictory observations and interpretations in contemporary sodium ion battery research, since debates on these controversies are likely to fuel future sodium battery research.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrwgKXFAPzwjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liok57obT_iQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXnslKhs7c%253D&amp;md5=c74372739d2eae295ff8891b7717cf2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/chem.202300009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">SnS-SnO2 Heterostructures Anchored on GO as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium Ion Battery</span>. <i>Chem.─Eur.         </div><div class="casAbstract">MoSe2, as a typical 2D material, possesses tremendous potential in Na-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to larger interlayer distance, more favorable band gap structure, and higher theor. specific capacity than other analogs.  Nevertheless, the low intrinsic electronic cond. and irreversible conversion of discharged products of Mo/Na2Se to MoSe2 seriously hamper its electrochem. performance.  Herein, through a facile hydrothermal method combined with calcination process, Sn-doped MoSe2 nanosheets grown on graphene substrate in the vertical direction are fabricated. An ultra-stable reversible specific capacity of 268.5 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 can be maintained after 1600 cycles.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have been emerging as a potential alternative to lithium-ion batteries, esp. for large-scale applications.  In this work, a hybrid of ultrasmall SnSb nanoparticles (the diam. &lt;2 nm) encapsulated in three-dimensional N-doped nanoporous carbon frameworks (SnSb/3D-NPC) was synthesized by a facile chem. redn. method.  To the best of our knowledge, this is the smallest SnSb nanoparticle ever reported.  As a sodium-ion battery anode, SnSb/3D-NPC delivers a high reversible capacity (693.6 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 100 cycles), superior rate performance (359.1 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) and cycling stability (266.6 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 15,000 cycles), which outperform other SnSb-based materials.  These remarkable performances originate from: (i) ultrasmall SnSb nanoparticles and their uniform distribution, which increase the sp. surface of electrodes and thus guarantee the full utilization of active materials, enhance pseudocapacitive contributions for Na storage, shorten Na+ diffusion distance, and reduce the strain during the sodiation/desodiation process; and (ii) the unique 3D integrated structure of SnSb/3D-NPC, which supplies a conductive network, efficient electrolyte diffusion paths and more active sites for Na+ insertion/extn., suppresses the aggregation of SnSb nanoparticles, and buffers large vol. change of SnSb through carbon nanocages during the cycling process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryNdOI04t0ubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liok57obT_iQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXovVaru78%253D&amp;md5=9f6209c24335ab4925b2286f32b76403</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2023.168950"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Verdianto, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.-O.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sandwich-like heterostructured SnSb/MXene composite anode for enhanced sodium-ion storage performance</span>. <i>J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-based dual-ion batteries (PDIBs) have shown good application prospects in large-scale energy storage systems.  However, because of the limited theor. capacity of carbonaceous anodes, the electrochem. performance of PDIBs reported at present is still unsatisfactory.  Employing alloy materials as anodes should be a possible way to improve the capacity of PDIBs.  Herein, free-standing porous carbon nanowires encapsulated with SnSb nanodots (SnSb@PCNWs) are first applied as the anodes for high-performance PDIBs.  The free-standing structure design can reduce the cost and increase the proportion of active materials.  Besides, the SnSb nanodots provide high potassium storage capacity, while the porous carbon nanowires can effectively buffer the vol. expansion of SnSb nanodots.  Consequently, the optimized PDIBs display high capacity of 255.3 mAh g-1 at 2 C (based on anodes), outstanding rate capability up to 12 C, and good cycling performance for 300 cycles at 10 C, which are the best results of the reported PDIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrRgdyP_Ok-7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liok57obT_iQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXisVGrsrvF&amp;md5=9c545ca150546b4925f89880ae66ae34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202002297"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitlin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Review of Emerging Concepts in SEI Analysis and Artificial SEI Membranes for Lithium, Sodium, and Potassium Metal Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">43</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2002297</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202002297</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Review of emerging concepts in solid electrolyte interphase analysis and artificial solid electrolyte interphase membranes for lithium, sodium, and potassium metal battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Wei; Liu, Pengcheng; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Anodes for lithium metal batteries, sodium metal batteries, and potassium metal batteries are susceptible to failure due to dendrite growth.  This review details the structure-chem.-performance relations in membranes that stabilize the anodes solid electrolyte interphase (SEI), allowing for stable electrochem. plating/stripping.  Case studies involving Li, Na, and K are presented to illustrate key concepts. "Classical" vs. "modern" understandings of the SEI are described, with an emphasis on the new structural insights obtained through novel anal. techniques, including in situ liq.-secondary ion mass spectroscopy, titrn. gas chromatog., and tip-enhanced Raman spectroscopy.  This Review highlights diverse approaches for increasing SEI stability, either by inserting a secondary layer between the native SEI and the separator, or by combining the membrane with a native SEI to form a hybrid composite.  Exciting and nonintuitive findings are discussed, such as that the metal anode roughness profoundly affects the SEI structure and stability, or that org. artificial SEI-layers may be more effective than the native inorg.-org. SEIs.  Emerging multifunctional architectures are presented, which serve a dual role as metal hosts and metal surface protection layers.  Throughout the Review, fruitful future research directions and the crit. areas where there is incomplete understanding are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoAhCbqYw6U8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liok57obT_iQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvF2jur7L&amp;md5=db6729710066d97907575e4a3559ec35</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202214258"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrostatic Shielding Boosts Electrochemical Performance of Alloy-Type Anode Materials of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries show promising potential for large-scale energy storage.  However, the large size and heavy mass of Na+ always results in huge vol. change and inferior electrochem. stability, esp. in alloy-type anode materials.  Here, mol. engineering of the polymer binders, i.e., crosslinking of poly(acrylic acid) with glycerin (PAA-GLY), reinforces the mech. properties, eliminates the active protons of PAA, and benefits electrolyte diffusion, thereby remarkably improving electrochem. performance.  Using μ-Sn as an example, the cycle life at 2 A g-1 is extended from ≈26 cycles of PAA to ≈2000 cycles of PAA-GLY.  Meanwhile, the initial Coulombic efficiency is promoted to 90.3%, allowing the fabrication step of electrode presodiation for full cells to be eliminated.  Thus, the full cells run 300 cycles at 2 A g-1.  In addn., the binder allows the thick electrode to exhibit an areal capacity of 6.8 mAh cm-2.  This binder is also applied for μ-Bi and μ-Sb.  The simple operation, remarkable improvement, and wide applications indicate the promising prospects of this strategy for advanced electrodes in sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoGTNCqhoL2cbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhl_rcNgm_r4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XjtFSksrbL&amp;md5=4c61f86680f7bc6d53057ffd0e331ab5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1039/D2CC00833E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bimetallic Bi-Sn microspheres as high initial coulombic efficiency and long lifespan anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are developed to address the serious concern about the limited resources of lithium.  To achieve high energy d., anode materials with a large specific capacity and a low operation voltage are highly desirable.  Herein, microsized particles of gray Sn (α-Sn) are explored as an anode material of SIBs for the first time.  The distinct structure of α-Sn endows it the reduced vol. change, the improved interaction with polymer binders and the in situ formation of amorphous Sn, as supported by in situ XRD, TEM and DFT calcns.  Therefore, α-Sn exhibits an excellent electrochem. performance, much better than β-Sn widely used before.  Even microsized particles of α-Sn without any treatments deliver a capacity of ~ 451 mAh g-1 after 3500 cycles at 2 A g-1 or ~ 464 mAh g-1 at 4 A g-1 in a rate test.  The results indicate the promising potential of α-Sn in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomNMw5cmJQS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhl_rcNgm_r4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFShtrjE&amp;md5=632cb9940fdec1f89a9118c0110497d2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.6b00491"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mogensen, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brandell, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Younesi, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solubility of the Solid Electrolyte Interphase (SEI) in Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Energy Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1173</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1178</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solubility of the Solid Electrolyte Interphase (SEI) in Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mogensen, Ronnie; Brandell, Daniel; Younesi, Reza</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is often stated that formation of a functional solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) in sodium ion batteries is hampered by the higher soly. of SEI components such as sodium salts in comparison to the lithium analogs.  In order to investigate these phenomena, SEI formation and functionality, as well as cell self-discharge, are studied for the sodium ion system with comparative expts. on the equiv. lithium ion system.  By conducting a set of expts. on carbonaceous anodes, the impact of SEI dissoln. is tested.  The results show that the SEI layer in sodium ion cells is inferior to that in lithium ion counterparts with regards to self-discharge; sodium cells show a loss in capacity at a dramatic rate as compared to the lithium counterparts when they are stored at sodiated and lithiated states, resp., for a long time with no external applied current or potential.  Also, synchrotron-based hard XPS measurements indicate that the major factor leading to increased self-discharge is dissoln. of significant parts of the sodium-based SEI.  Furthermore, the effect of fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) electrolyte additive on self-discharge is tested as part of the work.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokiL-DGoBWJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhl_rcNgm_r4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvVWnu7nN&amp;md5=efb6371771df6ea383fed6449e8e5e1e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702724"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goktas, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bolli, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Berg, E.                         rightTab-cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Modulating Electron Conducting Properties at Lithium Anode Interfaces for Durable Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Qi; Zhao, Kaixin; Wang, Jiahui; Xiao, Junpeng; Wu, Lili; Zhang, Xueqiang; Kong, Long; Li, Lu; Lu, Huiqing; Xie, Ying; Li, Wenjie; Zhang, Xitian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The lithium (Li) ion and electron diffusion behaviors across the actual solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) play a crit. role in regulating the Li nucleation and growth and improving the performance of lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries.  To date, a no. of researchers have pursued an SEI with high Li-ion cond. while ignoring the Li dendrite growth caused by electron tunneling in the SEI.  Herein, an artificial anti-electron tunneling layer with enriched lithium fluoride (LiF) and sodium fluoride (NaF) nanocrystals is constructed using a facile soln.-soaking method.  As evidenced theor. and exptl., the LiF/NaF artificial SEI exhibits an outstanding electron-blocking capability that can reduce electron tunneling, resulting in dendrite-free and dense Li deposition beneath the SEI, even with an ultrahigh areal capacity.  In addn., the artificial anti-electron tunneling layer exhibits improved ionic cond. and mech. strength, compared to those of routine SEI.  The sym. cells with protected Li electrodes achieve a stable cycling of 1500 h.  The LiF/NaF artificial SEI endows the Li-S full cells with long-term cyclability under conditions of high sulfur loading, lean electrolyte, and limited Li excess.  This study provides a perspective on the design of the SEI for highly safe and practical Li-S batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqbc3CFiePQQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhl_rcNgm_r4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XivFWqtrzO&amp;md5=ab01211bcc1b012d6d0be344ef729d9e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.0c12051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electroless Formation of a Fluorinated Li/Na Hybrid Interphase for Robust Lithium Anodes</span>. <i>J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineering a stable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is one of the crit. maneuvers in improving the performance of a lithium anode for high-energy-d. rechargeable lithium batteries.  Herein, we build a fluorinated lithium/sodium hybrid interphase via a facile electroless electrolyte-soaking approach to stabilize the repeated plating/stripping of lithium metal.  Jointed exptl. and computational characterizations reveal that the fluorinated hybrid SEI mainly consisting of NaF, LiF, LixPOyFz, and org. components features a mosaic polycryst. structure with enriched grain boundaries and superior interfacial properties toward Li.  This LiF/NaF hybrid SEI exhibits improved ionic cond. and mech. strength in comparison to the SEI without NaF.  Remarkably, the fluorinated hybrid SEI enables an extended dendrite-free cycling of metallic Li over 1300 h at a high areal capacity of 10 mAh cm-2 in sym. cells.  Furthermore, full cells based on the LiFePO4 cathode and hybrid SEI-protected Li anode sustain long-term stability and good capacity retention (96.70% after 200 cycles) at 0.5 C.  This work could provide a new avenue for designing robust multifunctional SEI to upgrade the metallic lithium anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokydiLqb-nQrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhl_rcNgm_r4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXjvFensro%253D&amp;md5=76078582a8c2b9abd2a79cfdeb52e2ec</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202200475"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, P.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, S.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrode-Electrolyte Interfacial Chemistry Modulation for Ultra-High Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries capable of operating at rate and temp. extremes are highly desirable, but elusive due to the dynamics and thermodn. limitations.  Herein, a strategy of electrode-electrolyte interfacial chem. modulation is proposed.  The com. hard carbon demonstrates superior rate performance with 212 mAh g-1 at an ultra-high c.d. of 5 A g-1 in the electrolyte with weak ion solvation/desolvation, which is much higher than those in common electrolytes (nearly no capacity in carbonate-based electrolytes).  Even at -20°C, a high capacity of 175 mAh g-1 (74% of its room-temp. capacity) can be maintained at 2 A g-1.  Such an electrode retains 90% of its initial capacity after 1000 cycles.  As proven, weak ion solvation/desolvation of THF greatly facilitates fast-ion diffusion at the SEI/electrolyte interface and homogeneous SEI with well-distributed NaF and org. components ensures fast Na+ diffusion through the SEI layer and a stable interface.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqdIVcdn7NorrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgPFyAwwiRH3g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xms1yhur8%253D&amp;md5=ea2a3f80a3c080c3cc6276b22f89da3c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201703576"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bommier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolytes, SEI Formation, and Binders: A Review of Nonelectrode Factors for Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Small.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">16</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e1703576</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
